译者注：每次看到这个视频里 Abelson 教授所展现出的对教育和开放资源事业的热忱，以
及他的国际主义胸怀，我都会十分感动。他和他的导师、同僚和学生们对世界的贡献，是一
份来自全球化进程蒸蒸日上、充满技术乐观主义的时代的馈赠，这份馈赠我们受益至今。

---

{{< track-segment start="00:00:00.000" end="00:00:03.200" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}INTERVIEWER: Today is August 23, 2011.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}采访者：今天是 2011 年 8 月 23 日。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:00:05.280" end="00:00:06.500" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}I'm Chris Boebel.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}我是 Chris Boebel。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:00:06.500" end="00:00:09.430" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}As part of the MIT150 Infinite History project, we're talking with professor Hal Abelson.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}作为“麻省理工学院 150 年无限历史项目” 的一部分，我们正在与 Hal Abelson 教授进行访谈。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:00:11.610" end="00:00:14.430" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}Professor Abelson is the Class of 1922 professor of electrical engineering and computer science at MIT.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}Abelson 教授是麻省理工学院（MIT）1922 （原文如此）届电气工程与计算机科学教授。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:00:17.430" end="00:00:21.140" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}He holds an AB degree from Princeton University and a PhD degree in mathematics from MIT.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}他拥有普林斯顿大学的文学学士学位和麻省理工学院的数学博士学位。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:00:23.860" end="00:00:27.320" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}In 1992, Abelson was designated as one of MIT's six inaugural MacVicar Faculty Fellows.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}1992 年，Abelson 被任命为麻省理工学院首批六位 MacVicar 教师研究员之一。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:00:30.150" end="00:00:32.259" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}Professor Abelson is co-director of the MIT-Microsoft iCampus Research Alliance in educational technology.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}Abelson 教授是 MIT-微软 iCampus 教育技术研究联盟的联合主任。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:00:36.450" end="00:00:39.130" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}He's co-chair of the MIT Council on Educational Technology.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}他是麻省理工学院教育技术委员会（MIT Council on Educational Technology） 的共同主席。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:00:39.830" end="00:00:41.820" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}And he serves on the steering committee of the HP-MIT Alliance.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}同时也在惠普-麻省理工学院（HP-MIT） 联盟的指导委员会任职。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:00:43.705" end="00:00:46.950" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}He has played key roles in fostering MIT institutional initiatives such as MIT OpenCourseWare and DSpace.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}他在推动麻省理工学院的院校倡议中发挥了关键作用，例如 MIT OpenCourseWare 和 DSpace。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:00:50.690" end="00:00:52.600" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}Hal, thanks very much for taking the time--{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}Hal，非常感谢您能抽出时间——{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:00:52.600" end="00:00:52.730" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}ABELSON: Sure.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}ABELSON：没问题。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:00:52.730" end="00:00:54.900" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}INTERVIEWER: --to talk today.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}采访者：——参加今天的谈话。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:00:54.900" end="00:00:57.320" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}So let's start at the beginning.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}那么让我们从头开始吧。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:00:57.320" end="00:00:58.310" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}ABELSON: The beginning?{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}ABELSON：从头开始？{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:00:58.310" end="00:01:00.185" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}INTERVIEWER: The beginning.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}采访者：是的，从头开始。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:01:00.185" end="00:01:03.120" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}Just start by telling me a little bit about where you grew up and the early years?{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}请先跟我聊聊您是在哪里长大的， 以及早年的生活？{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:01:07.950" end="00:01:10.470" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}ABELSON: So the real early years, I grew up on a chicken farm in central New Jersey.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}ABELSON：真正的早年时期，我是在新泽西州中部的一个养鸡场长大的。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:01:13.160" end="00:01:16.370" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}My parents worked on the farm.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}我的父母在农场工作。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:01:18.120" end="00:01:22.660" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}My father later went and worked in the post office.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}我父亲后来去了邮局工作。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:01:22.660" end="00:01:25.810" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}I was the first one in my family to go to college, although my parents were always very, very interested in education.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}我是家里第一个上大学的人， 但是我的父母一直对教育非常、非常感兴趣。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:01:31.300" end="00:01:33.415" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}My parents liked music, education.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}我的父母喜欢音乐和教育。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:01:33.415" end="00:01:38.220" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}I had an uncle who sort of was the college person, who worked for Exxon and had a high level position there.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}我有一位叔叔算是家里读过大学的人，他在 Exxon（埃克森公司）工作并担任高管。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:01:41.210" end="00:01:44.250" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}So we always cared a lot about education.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}所以我们一直非常重视教育。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:01:44.250" end="00:01:48.730" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}I'm not quite sure where I glommed onto math and science.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}我不太确定自己是从哪里开始迷上数学和科学的。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:01:48.730" end="00:01:52.730" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}I remember when I was I guess 12 or 13, I decided I wanted to be a physicist, mostly because I think I liked the word.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}我记得大概在十二三岁的时候，我决定我想成为一名物理学家，主要是因为我喜欢这个词。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:01:56.590" end="00:01:57.940" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}But I didn't know what that was.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}但我当时并不了解那究竟是什么。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:01:57.940" end="00:02:02.310" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}I did sort of okay in school.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}我在学校的表现还算可以。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:02:04.500" end="00:02:07.440" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}When I talk to kids these days, I remind them that when I was their age in seventh or eighth grade, I was getting D's in mathematics.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}如今我和孩子们交谈时，会提醒他们，当我像他们那么大，读七八年级的时候，我的数学成绩是 D。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:02:14.130" end="00:02:16.190" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}In fact, like a lot of people who end up going into computers, we are really bad at doing arithmetic.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}事实上，就像许多最终进入计算机领域的人一样，我们其实非常不擅长算术。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:02:20.590" end="00:02:23.240" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}Someone once said the reason a lot of people go into computers is to make up for their own handicaps in doing that.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}有人曾说，很多人进入计算机领域的原因是为了弥补自己在这方面的不足。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:02:27.000" end="00:02:30.060" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}So I wasn't particularly good in any of those subjects early on.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}所以早期我在这些科目上表现得并不是特别好。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:02:31.010" end="00:02:35.150" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}And then about the time I got in high school, I started being good at it.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}然后大约到了上高中的时候，我开始变得擅长这些了。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:02:38.370" end="00:02:43.020" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}One of the things the school did, they hired somebody to help me learn calculus because of course our school did nothing like that.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}学校当时做的一件事是雇人来教我微积分，因为我们学校当然没有这样的课程。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:02:48.480" end="00:02:51.460" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}And I don't know, sort of grew a lot of interest in math and science from there.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}然后不知怎的，我从那时起开始对数学和科学产生了浓厚的兴趣。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:02:53.120" end="00:02:54.640" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}So at some point I said gee, I don't want to be a physicist anymore.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}所以在某个时刻，我说，哎呀，我不再想当物理学家了。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:02:56.470" end="00:02:59.990" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}I want to be a mathematician because I guess that word sounded better.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}我想成为一名数学家，因为我觉得这个词听起来更棒。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:03:01.990" end="00:03:08.050" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}And then I got into Princeton on a scholarship, which was nice because my family could never have afforded anything like that.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}后来我拿了奖学金进入普林斯顿大学，那样很好， 因为我的家庭根本负担不起那样的事情。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:03:13.100" end="00:03:15.020" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}And did pretty well at Princeton.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}我在普林斯顿表现得相当不错。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:03:15.020" end="00:03:17.840" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}Started getting interested in a subject called algebraic topology.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}我开始对一门叫作代数拓扑（algebraic topology）的学科产生兴趣。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:03:21.730" end="00:03:25.390" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}And then got into MIT graduate school on that.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}凭借这个研究方向，被 MIT 研究生院录取。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:03:25.390" end="00:03:31.360" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}And ended up coming to graduate school at MIT mostly because my wife and I were looking for places we could both go.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}最终决定来 MIT 读研，主要是因为我和妻子当时在寻找两人都能去的地方。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:03:38.930" end="00:03:42.460" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}We weren't married then, but she was looking for a place where she could go.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}那时我们还没结婚，但她在找一个她能去的地方。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:03:42.990" end="00:03:44.700" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}She got into BU's School of Social Work.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}她去了 BU（波士顿大学）的社会工作学院。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:03:44.700" end="00:03:46.800" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}I got into MIT.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}我去了 MIT。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:03:46.800" end="00:03:49.350" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}MIT also had a draft deferment.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}MIT 当时还提供兵役缓征。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:03:49.350" end="00:03:53.310" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}So back in ancient days, one of the things that you wanted to do was if you were worried that getting drafted to go to the Vietnam War, so MIT did something where I think because I was teaching or something like that, there was a category of draft deferment you could get.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}所以在那个久远的年代，假如你担心被征召参加越南战争，你想做的事情之一就是， MIT 有个政策，应该是因为我在做教学或类似的工作，你可以获得某类兵役缓征。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:04:05.930" end="00:04:08.040" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}So we ended up coming to MIT.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}所以我们最终来到了 MIT。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:04:08.040" end="00:04:13.280" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}And MIT was just absolutely an fascinating place.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}MIT 绝对是一个非常迷人的地方。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:04:13.280" end="00:04:18.290" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}One of the nicest things, when I first showed up at MIT, we lived in Westgate.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}最美好的事情之一是，当我刚来到 MIT 时，我们住在 Westgate。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:04:19.930" end="00:04:23.620" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}And one of the great memories that we had of being in Westgate was looking down over the field and at the other end of the field, seeing the tear gas on Mass Ave. Because that was the time when even MIT students were protesting stuff.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}在 Westgate 最棒的回忆之一就是俯瞰球场，在另一端，看到麻省大道（Mass Ave.）上的催泪瓦斯。因为那是连 MIT 的学生都在抗议的时代。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:04:37.160" end="00:04:40.530" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}They were protesting, for anybody who remembers, Draper Labs used to be called the Institute Labs.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}他们抗议的是，如果有人还记得的话， Draper 实验室曾经叫学院实验室。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:04:43.370" end="00:04:47.060" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}And there was a protest about how is it that on the MIT campus, there was classified research related to the Vietnam War?{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}抗议的内容是，为什么 MIT 的校园里， 会有与越南战争相关的机密研究？{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:04:53.280" end="00:04:54.280" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}It was just sort of wonderful.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}那真实挺奇妙的。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:04:54.280" end="00:04:57.170" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}Just marvelous to be here and look through this thing.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}人在这里，目睹这一切，真是不可思议。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:04:57.170" end="00:04:59.970" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}And what do I remember of MIT?{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}我对 MIT 还有什么记忆呢？{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:04:59.970" end="00:05:05.080" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}I remember going up to the door on 77 Mass Ave. And gosh, they were automatic doors.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}

{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}采访者：那么稍微回溯一下，你在那之前在普林斯顿， 甚至更早之前，做过计算机科学方面的工作吗？{{< /styled-paragraph >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:07:42.040" end="00:07:45.720" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}But at Princeton, a bunch of us worked in the computer center.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}但在普林斯顿，我们一群人在计算机中心工作。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:07:48.450" end="00:07:53.905" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}And the Princeton Computer Center had an IBM--{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}普林斯顿计算机中心有一台 IBM ——{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:07:53.905" end="00:07:56.110" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}I think a 7.090 or 7.10.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}应该是 7.090 或 7.10。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:07:56.110" end="00:07:59.880" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}It got one of the first 3.60s.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}它搞到了最早的 3.60 之一。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:07:59.880" end="00:08:03.030" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}And they were working on this very weird thing called time sharing.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}他们当时在研究一种非常奇怪的东西， 叫作分时系统（time sharing）。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:08:07.630" end="00:08:12.250" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}And a bunch of us went around and messed around with that and did what most of Princeton considered to be a totally worthless, stupid thing with computers, which is actually using it for text processing.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}我们一群人在上面四处摆弄，捣鼓普林斯顿大多数人认为是完全不值得用计算机做的蠢事——那就是用它进行文本处理。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:08:24.790" end="00:08:28.010" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}Because everyone knew that what computers were really for were solving big complicated equations.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}因为那时众所周知，计算机真正的用途是求解复杂大型方程式。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:08:30.940" end="00:08:34.460" >}}

{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}计算机中心以前每周会停机几个小时， 让我们那些想要瞎胡闹、浪费时间的家伙去摆弄这种文本编辑玩意儿。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:08:42.490" end="00:08:45.570" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}Get tremendous complaints from the astrophysics department because people had to stop trying to solve on science equations.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}结果受到了天体物理学系的巨量投诉， 因为他们被迫停下来对科学方程式的求解尝试。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:08:48.480" end="00:08:49.720" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}So I became one of the people who were messing around with that.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}所以，我成了那些瞎鼓捣这东西的人之一。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:08:50.810" end="00:08:53.710" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}And I became a little bit of a consultant, an undergraduate consultant in the computer system, teaching people to migrate their programs from FORTRAN to a language that IBM and a couple of other places were pushing then called PL/1, a very modest name, Programming Language 1.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}我后来有点像顾问，读本科的计算机系统顾问， 教人们把他们的程序从 FORTRAN 迁移到 IBM 和其他一些地方当时推崇的语言， 叫作 PL/1，一个非常谦虚的名字， “编程语言 1”。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:09:11.980" end="00:09:15.020" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}And this was supposed to be the be all and end all of the new computer stuff.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}在设想中，它应该是一个终极解决方案， 不再需要其它的计算机创新了。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:09:15.840" end="00:09:19.610" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}And there was a big move to say you should translate all your programs into PL/1.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}当时有一种趋势，主张你应该将所有的程序都转换成 PL/1。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:09:20.680" end="00:09:25.130" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}So I became one of what was called the PL/1 kids and would consult with faculty in the other departments about how to modify their programs.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}所以我成了所谓的“PL/1 小子”之一， 为其他部门的教职员工提供咨询，看怎么修改他们的程序。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:09:31.650" end="00:09:33.920" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}So I had some stuff in computing and I knew about that.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}所以我确实接触过一些计算方面的东西， 也有所自知。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:09:35.940" end="00:09:40.610" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}I knew very little about what I actually went into at MIT.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}对于我后来在 MIT 真正从事的领域，我当时知之甚少。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:09:40.610" end="00:09:43.360" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}But it was a background in computers, enough to walk into the AI Lab and do interesting things.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}但那段计算机背景足以让我走进 AI Lab 去做些有趣的事情。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:09:47.600" end="00:09:50.030" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}INTERVIEWER: But at the time you came to MIT, initially there was not a sense that you would be moving in that direction?{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}采访者：但你来 MIT 的时候， 最初并没有感觉到你会朝那个方向发展？{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:09:53.770" end="00:09:55.660" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}ABELSON: No, I was in the math department.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}ABELSON：没有，我当时在数学系。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:09:55.660" end="00:10:01.880" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}And I was a graduate student in the math department, became an instructor in the math department after that, and only moved into computing later on because some of the work I was doing in topology was related to distributed computing.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}我是数学系的研究生，之后在数学系担任讲师，后来才转向计算领域， 因为我当时从事的一部分拓扑学（topology）工作与分布式计算有关。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}

{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:15:18.360" end="00:15:21.560" >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:20:10.590" end="00:20:14.460" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}One was Ben Snyder, who wrote a very famous book at MIT called The Hidden Curriculum, which is all about how surviving at MIT is a process of constant triage.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}一位是 Ben Snyder，他写了一本在 MIT 非常有名的书，叫做《隐藏的课程》（The Hidden Curriculum）， 讲的是在 MIT 生存是一个不断取舍的过程。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:20:22.630" end="00:20:25.100" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}And students at MIT have to learn that.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}MIT 的学生必须了解这一点。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:20:25.100" end="00:20:29.000" >}}

{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}一位是 Don Schon，他在斯隆学院（Sloan School）， 以他的知识理论，或说“信奉知识”（espoused knowledge） 与实际行动之间关系的思想而闻名。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}

{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}第三个是 Seymour，做 Logo 相关的工作。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:20:37.030" end="00:20:40.125" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}So I became part of the Division for Study in Research and Education.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}于是，我成为了科研与教育研究部的一员。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:20:42.170" end="00:20:47.140" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}Got a joint appointment in math and DSRE.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}获得了数学系和 DSRE 的联合职务。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:20:47.140" end="00:20:51.250" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}And that's where we sort of really started to do Logo work as sort of real MIT research kind of stuff.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}在那儿，我们开始真正将 Logo 工作作为 MIT 的正式研究项目来开展。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:20:56.070" end="00:20:57.910" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}But then eventually what happens, MIT decided to close down DSRE.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}但最终发生的情况是，MIT 决定解散 DSRE。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:20:59.270" end="00:21:04.730" >}}

{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}我当时资历太浅，还无法理解甚至没意识到这背后的政治因素。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:21:06.930" end="00:21:09.410" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}But in any case, MIT decided to close it down.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}但无论如何，MIT 决定关闭它。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:21:09.410" end="00:21:12.110" >}}

{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}然后我进入了电气工程与计算机科学系，大概是因为 Logo 上的工作，也因为当时我正在做分布式计算。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:21:20.590" end="00:21:24.710" >}}

{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}后来我就一直在那里。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}

{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}ABELSON：嗯，我其实不太把 Logo 和分布式计算放在一起考虑。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}

{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:21:48.810" end="00:21:52.700" >}}

{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}ABELSON：除了它们最后都成为了对计算的某种愿景，而且都很形式化等等。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:21:56.100" end="00:21:59.950" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}The Logo work was as I said, magic.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}Logo 的工作就像我说的，是魔法。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:21:59.950" end="00:22:04.850" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}It is really hard right now to go back.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}现在很难回到那个时代了。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:22:04.850" end="00:22:10.961" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}We're talking a dozen years before the personal computer.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}我们在谈论的是个人计算机出现前的十几年的事情。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:22:10.961" end="00:22:17.980" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}What we used to say in Logo is oh my god, if a computer could just cost $10,000, that would revolutionize all of education.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}我们以前做 Logo 的时候经常说，老天爷，如果一台电脑只要 1 万美元， 那必将对教育产生彻底变革。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:22:24.095" end="00:22:26.680" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}Because what we were doing is these were million machines, a million dollars in 1968 dollars.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}因为那时我们用的是几百万美元的机器， 1968 年的几百万。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:22:35.530" end="00:22:37.690" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}They were sitting in the Artificial Intelligence Lab, doing the world's very best, fanciest research an artificial intelligence.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}它们放在人工智能实验室里， 做着世界上最顶尖、最前沿的人工智能研究。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:22:43.470" end="00:22:47.820" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}And we were hooking them up over phone lines to be used by sixth graders in Lexington, Massachusetts.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}而我们却把它们连上电话线，供马萨诸塞州列克星敦的六年级学生使用。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:22:52.930" end="00:22:55.700" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}And just a totally outrageous thing.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}离谱至极的事情。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:22:55.700" end="00:22:59.220" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}One my first projects as a graduate student was working on a remote display that you could hook up that could sit in Lexington and move over a phone line.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}我作为研究生的第一个项目之一，就是做一种可以连接的远程显示器，它可以放在列克星敦，通过电话线传输。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:23:07.070" end="00:23:10.680" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}And so students could write what was effectively the first Logo turtle and draw designs on this graphics display.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}让学生们能编写出事实上的第一个 Logo 海龟程序，在这个图形显示器上绘制图案。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:23:14.720" end="00:23:17.530" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}So that was like my first job as a graduate student, implementing that.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}那是我作为研究生的第一份工作， 实现那个东西。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:23:19.190" end="00:23:22.060" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}But it was so off scale.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}但它太超出常规了。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:23:22.060" end="00:23:28.510" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}Just the very idea that a computer would be something that a kid could use.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}就是这个“计算机要让孩子能用”的想法。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:23:29.780" end="00:23:35.570" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}We take it so it for granted now that it's almost impossible to put yourself in that mindset.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}我们现在对此习以为常，以至于几乎不可能代入那种思维模式当中。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:23:38.300" end="00:23:43.940" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}So most people thought we were crazy, because I mean what a weird thing.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}大多数人觉得我们疯了，因为我是说， 这事太奇怪了。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:23:44.440" end="00:23:47.810" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}Why could a computer ever be something that would be relevant to a kid, much less programming it or anything?{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}计算机怎么可能与儿童相关， 更别说去给它编程了。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:23:52.030" end="00:23:54.170" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}And it was a mixture of what happened in the AI Lab.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}这些混在一起，发生在人工智能实验室里。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:23:54.170" end="00:23:57.270" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}Every couple of weeks somebody would run in off the street saying, I want to see the robots.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}每隔几周就会有人从街上跑进来，说， 我想看看机器人。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:24:01.320" end="00:24:02.390" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}You're making robots.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}你们在造机器人。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:24:02.390" end="00:24:04.480" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}I want to come see them.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}我想要来看看它们。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:24:04.480" end="00:24:08.780" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}And AI Lab was just a wonderful mixture of that.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}当时的 AI 实验室就是那些的奇妙混合体。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:24:08.780" end="00:24:12.070" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}So it was run by Seymour Papert and of course Marvin Minsky, who are just two completely brilliant people with I think a real sense of faith, in that if you're surrounded by a lot of smart people and you give them a lot of freedom and your job is really to inspire people, it will do great things.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}它由 Seymour Papert 领导，当然还有 Marvin Minsky，他们是两位极其杰出人， 我认为他们真正有一种信念，如果你身边围绕着一群聪明人，给他们充分的自由， 你的工作实际是去启发他们，这样就能做出伟大的成就。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:24:35.500" end="00:24:40.600" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}And the AI Lab was just infused with that.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}人工智能实验室充满了这种理念。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:24:40.600" end="00:24:44.450" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}There was just a tremendous sense of community among the AI researchers, which was partly true because it was pretty small.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}人工智能研究人员之间有种强烈的社区意识，一部分原因是因为它相当小。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:24:48.890" end="00:24:52.570" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}One of the things that's happened more recently is that merged with the Lab for Computer Science.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}更近一些的时候，它与计算机科学实验室合并了。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:24:55.530" end="00:24:59.790" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}And it doesn't have that same real sense of community and flexibility.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}它不再有之前那种真正的社区意识和灵活性了。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:25:01.460" end="00:25:04.670" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}But the original AI Lab, there have been a much of books written about it, all sorts of things emerged from that.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}但是原来的人工智能实验室，已经有很多书写过了，各种各样的成功都起源于这些特点。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:25:07.190" end="00:25:09.760" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}The other thing that emerged from that, that maybe you want to talk about later is Richard Solomon and the whole free software movement, which these days is better known as the Open Source Movement.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}另一件源于这些特点的事情，也许你之后会想谈到，是 Richard Stallman 和整个自由软件运动，如今它更为人所知的名称是开源运动。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:25:18.950" end="00:25:22.280" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}But that was a thing--{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}但那是一件——{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:25:22.280" end="00:25:24.650" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}I mean in a deep sense it had to do with computer science, but not obviously.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}我是说，在深层意义上它与计算机科学有关， 但并不是很明显。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:25:25.500" end="00:25:29.360" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}But it's a whole kind of philosophy that grew out of this sense that technology is fundamentally a data community and fundamentally about a whole bunch of inspired people sharing and building on each other's work.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}它是一整套哲学，源于一种观念，认为技术本质上是一个数据社区，本质上是关于一群受启发的人彼此分享、在他人工作的基础上继续构建的事情。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:25:42.290" end="00:25:45.050" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}And that of course goes way past software into things like Creative Commons and lots of the stuff that we see now.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}而这一点远远超出了软件领域，延伸到了像知识共享（Creative Commons） 以及我们今天看到的许多事物中。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:25:48.270" end="00:25:52.820" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}But it came out of that germ of sharing around a technology community.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}但它起源于技术社区中分享的萌芽。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:25:55.300" end="00:25:57.810" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}INTERVIEWER: Yeah, I want to definitely in a little bit explore some of these broader ideas in their current form.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}采访者：是的，我肯定想要探讨下在当下形态中的这些更宽泛的理念。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:26:01.930" end="00:26:07.520" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}But let's talk a bit about that culture of sharing and of open networks within MIT at that point.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}但让我们先谈谈那时 MIT 里的那种共享和开放网络文化吧。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:26:13.900" end="00:26:17.480" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}I mean I've read that obviously there's a whole sort of different landscape of security and passwords or lack thereof.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}我的意思是我读到过，显然当时的安全和密码体系，或者说它们的缺失， 和现在截然不同。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:26:23.030" end="00:26:27.370" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}But just describe the environment a bit more at that time and how obviously it had effects later.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}但请再多描述下当时的环境，以及它是如何显而易见地对后来产生影响的。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:26:30.610" end="00:26:33.490" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}ABELSON: Well remember for thinking about now, the internet--{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}ABELSON：嗯，要知道站在现在的角度，互联网——{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:26:35.740" end="00:26:40.770" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}it wasn't an internet then-- the ARPANET was a small place.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}那时还称不上互联网——ARPANET 是一个很小的地方。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:26:40.770" end="00:26:43.780" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}And it really was a very small, very, very homogeneous place.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}它真的是一个非常小，非常、 非常同质化的地方。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:26:45.960" end="00:26:50.080" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}I like to tell people I've had my email address since I kind of knew all of the people that I could have send email to.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}我常常跟人说，自从我几乎认识所有可以互发邮件的人起，我就一直使用这个电子邮件地址。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:26:53.230" end="00:26:56.350" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}I mean it's been written a lot that people who originally designed the internet said they just sort of did not design the internet architecture to think that there would be bad guys out there.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}我是说有很多记录，最初设计互联网的人们说，他们设计互联网架构时根本没有考虑过那里会有坏人。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:27:08.990" end="00:27:10.220" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}Because they knew all the people.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}因为他们认识所有的人。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:27:10.220" end="00:27:12.220" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}All the people were like them.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}所有的人都和他们一样。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:27:12.220" end="00:27:14.410" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}And that reflected over in passwords.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}这一点也体现在了密码上。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:27:14.410" end="00:27:18.610" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}I remember there was one sort of dark day when the people from ARPA said, you need to put passwords on your accounts because they're on the network.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}我记得有那么一个“黑暗的日子”，ARPA 的人说， 你们必须给账户加上密码， 因为它们连网了。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:27:24.920" end="00:27:29.860" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}And for security, you need to do that.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}安全起见，你们必须这样做。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:27:29.860" end="00:27:32.740" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}And a whole bunch of us were just convinced this was a horrible idea.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}我们一大群人就坚信这是一个糟糕透顶的主意。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:33:54.560" end="00:33:57.810" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}So that's another kind of educational link that I was exposed to.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}所以那是我接触到的另一类与教育有关的连接。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:34:00.360" end="00:34:06.130" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}And later, my colleague Andy diSessa and I ran that kind of summer high school program at MIT around computer science and Logo and teaching things.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}后来，我和我的同事 Andy diSessa 在 MIT 举办过那种高中暑期项目，围绕计算机科学、 Logo 以及教学来展开。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:34:12.820" end="00:34:17.000" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}So I've been interested in education kind of from that perspective.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}所以从那个角度来看，我一直都对教育很感兴趣。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:34:18.250" end="00:34:21.710" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}I've also played around with computers in education.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}我也尝试过将计算机应用于教育。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:34:23.590" end="00:34:29.090" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}One of the things I did in the math department was I was teaching linear algebra.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}我在数学系做过的一件事是教线性代数的时候。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:34:30.074" end="00:34:33.130" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}And I think just for the heck of it, I did what must have been one of the very first MIT computer exercises where students used the Multics computer system in those days to do some exercise at the end of the day about matrices.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}我记得只是为了好玩，我设计了应该是 MIT 最早的计算机练习之一，让学生们使用当时的 Multics 计算机系统， 在一天结束时做一些关于矩阵的练习。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:34:45.460" end="00:34:47.389" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}Now I didn't know what I was doing.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}当时我并不知道自己在做什么。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:34:47.389" end="00:34:49.199" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}And it wasn't particularly good and wasn't particularly successful.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}它并不是特别出色，也不是特别成功。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:34:49.780" end="00:34:53.300" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}But it was kind of foray into saying, gosh these MIT computers might actually get used in courses.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}但那是一次初步的尝试说，老天，这些 MIT 的计算机或许真的能用在课程中。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:34:57.830" end="00:35:01.790" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}Not much of that happened for a long time after that though.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}不过在那之后很长一段时间里，没有太多类似的事情。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:35:01.790" end="00:35:05.900" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}INTERVIEWER: Thinking about teaching computer science specifically, can you talk a bit about the Structure and Interpretation of Computer Programs and what that grew out of and what the sort of fundamental concepts are behind your approach?{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}采访者：具体到计算机科学的教学， 能谈谈《计算机程序的构造和解释》 这本书，它的来源，以及你们教学方法背后的基本概念吗？{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:35:18.220" end="00:35:23.160" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}ABELSON: So Gerry Sussman and I, I think were really privileged in that we wrote a book that really was able to draw on that whole of a 20-year history of how MIT and that whole AI culture thought about computing.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}ABELSON：所以 Gerry Sussman 和我， 我觉得我们真的很荣幸能写这样一本书，它充分借鉴了整整 20 年来 MIT 以及整个人工智能文化圈对“计算”的思考。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:35:43.890" end="00:35:47.710" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}And it goes directly back to again Seymour Papert and Marvin Minsky.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}再一次，这又能直接追溯到 Seymour Papert 和 Marvin Minsky。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:35:49.450" end="00:35:53.600" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}And it really has to do with--{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}它的核心是——{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:35:53.600" end="00:35:57.500" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}what's the phrase we used-- a computer program is a way of expressing ideas and communicating ideas, and only incidentally about getting a machine to do stuff.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}我们怎么说的来着——计算机程序是表达想法和交流想法的手段， 让机器做事只是附带的结果。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:36:06.600" end="00:36:09.400" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}That is straight out of--{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}这直接源于——{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:36:09.400" end="00:36:11.290" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}I don't think Seymour used those words, but that's straight out of the Logo philosophy of we're teaching you--{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}Seymour 应该没有说过这句话，但这直接源于 Logo 的哲学：我们是在教你——{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:36:15.580" end="00:36:17.930" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}like I talked about juggling before.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}正如刚才谈到的抛接球一样。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:36:17.930" end="00:36:22.700" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}This really is, what's the procedure for how you juggle?{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}本质上是，抛接球到底是怎样的过程？{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:36:22.700" end="00:36:26.100" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}And critical in being able to do that is having the right set of words and having the right descriptive framework for saying things like that.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}要能教会它，至关重要的是拥有一套恰当的词汇和恰当的描述框架，来表达这类事情。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:36:33.310" end="00:36:39.700" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}And so the key idea in Structure and Interpretation is what we ended up calling the linguistic approach to programming design, which says if I would like to do some very complicated thing, one of the critical tasks is picking the right descriptive framework for saying that.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}所以《结构与解释》中的关键思想， 我们最终称之为“语言学方法”的程序设计， 意思是说如果我想做一些非常复杂的事情，关键任务之一是选择恰当的描述框架来表达它。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:36:58.080" end="00:37:00.990" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}So there is a complete blend.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}这是对之前那些想法的完全融合。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:37:00.990" end="00:37:08.560" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}I think somewhere in that book we wrote that when you make a complicated program, you're actually designing a special purpose computer language to solve a problem.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}我记得在书中某处我们写道，当你编写一个复杂的程序时，你实际上在设计一个专门的程序语言来解决问题。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:37:15.320" end="00:37:19.740" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}And it comes through in lots and lots of ways.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}这点体现在很多很多方面。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:37:19.740" end="00:37:25.190" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}So it goes back I think to the AI culture, which has the property that you don't quite know what problem you're solving because these things are really complicated.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}我觉得它起源于人工智能文化，它有一个特点是你不太清楚你要解决什么问题，因为它们非常复杂。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:37:31.000" end="00:37:37.020" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}It's not as if someone says compute the total payment on this mortgage where you know exactly what you're going to do.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}它不像有人让你计算出这笔抵押贷款的总还款额，你很清楚知道接下来要做什么。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:37:40.340" end="00:37:44.410" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}Rather it says, you want to be mucking around in this area to solve this problem and lots and lots and lots and lots of similar problems.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}相反，它是要你在这个领域摸索，来解决这个问题，以及很多、很多、很多、很多类似的问题。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:37:50.320" end="00:37:56.790" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}And that permeates both the design of the book and the actual programming technology that people use.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}这种理念既贯穿于本书的设计中， 也贯穿于人们实际使用的编程技术里。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:37:59.380" end="00:38:04.620" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}So the style of programming languages that go back to LISP is really sort of muddier.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}因此起源自 LISP 的编程语言风格是相当“浑浊”的。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:38:08.870" end="00:38:10.960" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}It's not a very precise kind of thing.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}它并不是种非常精确的东西。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:38:10.960" end="00:38:13.710" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}You make ways of programming things where you're solving not just one problem but a whole family of problems in that.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}你摸索出的编程方式，解决的不仅仅是一个问题，而是一整类问题。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:38:23.780" end="00:38:26.310" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}And again, it goes back to very, very technical things, like LISP is a very good language for creating other computer languages.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}这又再次源于一些非常、非常技术性的东西， 比如 LISP 这门语言非常适合用来创建其他计算机语言。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:38:32.070" end="00:38:33.760" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}Because when you're programming in LISP, you actually have the mentality of gosh, I'm actually creating some special purpose language to solve not just one problem, but lots of them.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}因为当你用 LISP 编程时，你实际上有一种心态，老天，我实际上是在创建某种专用语言，不仅是为了解决一个问题，而是为了解决很多问题。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:38:42.850" end="00:38:46.000" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}And that's the critical idea in Structure and Interpretation.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}而这正是《构造与解释》中的核心思想。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:38:47.250" end="00:38:49.940" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}I mean we can't take credit for that.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}我想说，这不是我们自己的发明。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:38:52.150" end="00:38:57.570" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}We were just blessed that there was a whole tradition of 20 years of really deep thinking at MIT and a couple of other similar places.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}我们只是很幸运，在 MIT 和其他几个类似的地方有整整 20 年的深度思考的传承。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:39:04.060" end="00:39:07.600" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}And we sort of got to be the people who got to put that in the book.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}而我们只是恰好成为了把那些思考写进书里的人。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:39:09.800" end="00:39:11.830" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}And it's had enormous influence, but it's not because of us, it's because the tremendous power of those ideas and the communities that they came from.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}这本书产生了巨大的影响，但那并不是因为我们个人，而是因为那些思想本身以及孕育出它们的那些社区所拥有的强大力量。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:39:17.900" end="00:39:21.750" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}INTERVIEWER: So moving beyond those communities that the book and that thought process came out of, did you encounter resistance, maybe that's not the right word, maybe misunderstanding--{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}采访者：那么，等走出孕育出这本书以及那种思考方式的社群之后，你们有没有遇到过阻力——也许这个词不太准确， 或许该说是误解——{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:39:28.880" end="00:39:30.735" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}people who were focused on the syntax?{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}从关注点在语法上的人那里？{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:39:30.735" end="00:39:33.380" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}ABELSON: So we published this with MIT Press.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}ABELSON：我们跟 MIT 出版社出版这本书后。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:39:33.380" end="00:39:38.280" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}And MIT Press sent it out for reviews.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}MIT 出版社把它送出去做评审。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:39:38.280" end="00:39:41.800" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}And the first review came back.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}回来的第一份评审意见。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:39:41.800" end="00:39:42.670" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}And I'll never forget.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}我永远都不会忘记。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:39:42.670" end="00:39:49.840" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}It said, quote, the question is, is in MIT Press publishing this book going to advance or set back computer science?{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}它写到，原话：“问题在是，MIT 出版社出版这本书，是会推动还是会阻碍计算机科学的发展？”{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:39:56.090" end="00:39:57.890" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}So there was a lot of resistance to this because it's just very different.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}所以当时对此有很多阻力，因为它实在太不一样了。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:39:58.780" end="00:40:02.480" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}And there's a lot of people who really don't believe in that approach, who really do think it's the wrong thing.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}有很多人真的不认同这种方法，真心认为这样不对。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:40:06.420" end="00:40:10.420" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}Because again, it's this notion of you don't actually focus on solving this problem very, very, very precisely.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}因为刚才讲的，它的理念是不要把关注点放在非常、非常、非常精确地解决某个问题。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:40:16.620" end="00:40:19.985" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}There's a whole movement in computer science, a tremendously respectable one, and it says a program is like the proof of a mathematical theorem.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}计算机科学界有一整派运动， 备受尊敬，它认为一段程序就像一段对数学定理的证明。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:40:29.285" end="00:40:34.170" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}And there are people who do prove things about programs.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}也确实有人在做关于程序的证明。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:40:34.170" end="00:40:37.800" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}That in some sense is the mainstream almost. Whereas we're saying well, a program is sort of like a language.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}从某种意义上说，那几乎就是主流思想。而我们却说，嗯，一段程序像是一门语言。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:40:40.470" end="00:40:41.850" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}Like you can say lots of things.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}好比你可以说很多事情。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:40:41.850" end="00:40:44.290" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}And I don't imagine I'm going to prove everything I'm going to say.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}我不认为我要证明我说的每件事。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:40:44.840" end="00:40:47.220" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}It's just that the great thing is I get to see all these different things.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}关键是，最棒的事情在于我能看到所有这些不同的事物。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:40:48.750" end="00:40:52.610" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}So we've had a lot of influence, but I wouldn't even say that we're mainstream, even now.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}所以我们产生了很大的影响，但我肯定不会说我们是主流，哪怕是现在。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:40:55.040" end="00:40:58.930" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}INTERVIEWER: From my limited experience when I think back to my computer programming classes, it was more like the mathematical theorem approach.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}采访者：从我有限的经验看，回忆起我上计算机编程课程时，它更像是那种数学定理的方法。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}

{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}有一次，电气工程与计算机科学系里有一个传统：系里在 50 年代末从电力工程转向信号工程的时候， 在 Ernie Guillemin 以及其他 MIT 那些传奇人物的带领下， 催生了一系列非常、非常有影响力的教材， 我想是在 50 年代末、60 年代初， 它们几乎为电气工程领域树立了学术标杆。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}

{{< track-segment start="00:45:09.860" end="00:45:13.310" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}So what happened in the department is the department kind of decided that the way students get introduced into the department should become more horizontal and less vertical, by which I mean when you go into the department before the new curriculum, there were a bunch of very intellectually deep courses.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}所以，系里发生的事情是， 系里某种程度上决定，学生进入这个系的引介方式应该变得更“横向”，而不是那么“纵向”，我的意思是，在新课程体系之前你进到系里的时候， 会有一系列极具智力深度的课程。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}

{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}So 6.001 really is a deep course in software engineering.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}

{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}那里有一种金字塔结构， 先是本科生实验室助理， 他们分组后由研究生助教监督， 研究生助教再分组后再由真正的课程教师监督。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}

{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}所以，与坐在那里听讲座相反，它是一种非常开放、互动的、基于项目的学习方式。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}

{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}甚至最早 Gerry Sussman 和我写的那本书，我们一直有种感觉， 给 MIT 写教科书，并不会真的指望能卖出很多，因为就我们那本书而言，老天， 我们是要讲计算机科学，而且第一章还带着微积分。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}

{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}整个倡议构筑于一个想法上，就是我们一定要展示 MIT 所有的课程， 因为你想展示的是， 你的榜样作用是——{{< /styled-paragraph >}}

{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}某个第三世界国家的教育部长可能想了解该国在化学工程领域应该做些什么。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="01:00:18.280" end="01:00:23.310" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}And then you sort of see displayed out before you is what MIT, the top institution in the world, thinks is chemical engineering.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}然后你就能看到展示在你面前的是 MIT，世界顶尖学府， 所理解的化学工程。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}

{{< track-segment start="01:00:28.700" end="01:00:32.070" >}}

{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}这是我们在创立 OpenCourseWare 时脑海中的想法。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}

{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}当然，事情并没有完全像那样发展， 因为我们发现，老天爷，有那么多人是真的想来学习化学工程，来看这些课程。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}

{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}但是回到最初的理想， 你是在把自己树立为榜样， 去影响那些决策者。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}

{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}而这不仅仅是技术上的责任，更是一种伦理责任，关乎你的行为方式和你对此的思考方式。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}

{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}你有义务确保它朝着正确的方向发展， 基于你对世界会如何演变、 互联网会如何演变的理解。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}

{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}这一整套服务精神对于这个社区的运作不可或缺。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}

{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}我知道当我第一次听说它的时候，也就是在刚宣布它时，我想在那之前肯定没有， 从我非常有限的视角来看，MIT 竟然会这样做，真是相当令人震惊。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}

{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}ABELSON: 是啊。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}

{{< track-segment start="01:02:08.430" end="01:02:11.110" >}}

{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}我对 OpenCourseWare 唯一的遗憾是，我们是在互联网泡沫达到顶峰后才宣布它的。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="01:02:16.370" end="01:02:26.040" >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}Again, if you go back to the late '90s, right, 1998, 1999, 2000, there was this sense, if you read in the educational technology press or the education news, that universities were sitting on a gold mine.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}又说回去，假如你回到 90 年代，对， 1998，1999，2000，当时有一种观点，如果你去读关于教育技术的媒体或者教育新闻， 说大学正坐在一座金矿上。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="01:02:36.980" end="01:02:44.170" >}}

{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}人们说大学可以带来实打实的 2 万亿美元的经济效益，把他们的教学材料拿出来放到网络上。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="01:02:50.500" end="01:02:57.670" >}}

{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}而我非常喜欢的是，在那种气候下，MIT 却说， 嘿，我们不要钱。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}

{{< track-segment start="01:03:00.350" end="01:03:05.790" >}}

{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}教育应当是参与到这个互动地做研究的社区，成为社区的一分子。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}

{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}我非常喜欢这个说法。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-en" >}}Now that came from kind of a different place.{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}不过，这个想法源于一个略有不同的情景。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< track-segment start="01:03:22.640" end="01:03:27.250" >}}

{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}那是一个构思精巧的故事，和我们在那个情景下希望能处于的位置非常契合。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}
{{< /track-segment >}}

{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}但实际上发生的是，当时担任教务长的 Bob Brown 成立了教育技术委员会（Council on Educational Technology）， 他和我在几年里共同主持这个委员会。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}

{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}而那又源于更早的一件事，如 Chuck Vest 会说的，他在 1997 年左右在全国各地做演讲。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}

{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}然后另一个委员会持相反意见，由 Nick Negroponte 和 Mike Dertouzos 领导， 基本上是说：老天，MIT 是世界上最棒的地方。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}

{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}这两个委员当时算是僵持不下。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}

{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}而技术委员会则说，喔，这事实际关乎 MIT 的精神。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}

{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}所以 Bob Brown 是想找个办法来调和这些分歧，在审视这些情况时， 思考未来的路该怎么走。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}

{{< track-segment start="01:05:34.380" end="01:05:39.280" >}}

{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}于是他成立了教育技术委员会（Council on Educational Technology）， 它多少有点隐藏的议题就是要这么做，找到一条出路。{{< /styled-paragraph >}}

{{< track-segment start="01:05:43.460" end="01:05:52.020" >}}

{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}所以我们做的一件事是，我们真的请来了麦肯锡（McKinsey）做咨询——{{< /styled-paragraph >}}

{{< styled-paragraph class="lang-cn" >}}他们那种标准的战略咨询， 说我们的方向是什么，有哪些机遇？{{< /styled-paragraph >}}

{{< /track-segment >}}
